## ἴαμα (id: 002393000000000)

ἴαμα
====

ἴαμα (G2386)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-τος 

|  |
| --- |

 ἰάομαι

23\.138 · Physiological Processes and States · Health, Vigor, Strength

the power to heal, the capacity to heal (derivative of ἰάομαι\[a] ‘to cause to be well again, to heal,’ [23\.136](#23.136)) the capacity to cause someone to become healed or cured In some languages it may be difficult to speak of ‘giving the power to heal.’ A more natural form of expression is ‘cause to be able to heal.’

[1CO 12:9](https://ref.ly/Rom12:9) · [1CO 12:28](https://ref.ly/Rom12:28) · [1CO 12:30](https://ref.ly/Rom12:30)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 12:9; 1 Corinthians 12:28; 1 Corinthians 12:30

## ἰάομαι (id: 002397000000000)

ἰάομαι
======

ἰάομαι (G2390)

ἴαμα · ἴασις · ἰατρός

23\.136 · Physiological Processes and States · Health, Vigor, Strength

to heal, to cure, to make well, healing to cause someone to become well again after having been sick1 In a number of languages there are different terms for ‘healing’ depending upon the type of sickness or illness which is involved.

[MAT 8:8](https://ref.ly/Matt8:8) · [MAT 8:13](https://ref.ly/Matt8:13) · [MAT 15:28](https://ref.ly/Matt15:28) · [MRK 5:29](https://ref.ly/Matt5:29) · [LUK 5:17](https://ref.ly/Mark5:17) · [LUK 6:18](https://ref.ly/Mark6:18) · [LUK 6:19](https://ref.ly/Mark6:19) · [LUK 7:7](https://ref.ly/Mark7:7) · [LUK 8:47](https://ref.ly/Mark8:47) · [LUK 9:2](https://ref.ly/Mark9:2) · [LUK 9:11](https://ref.ly/Mark9:11) · [LUK 9:42](https://ref.ly/Mark9:42) · [LUK 14:4](https://ref.ly/Mark14:4) · [LUK 17:15](https://ref.ly/Mark17:15) · [LUK 22:51](https://ref.ly/Mark22:51) · [JHN 4:47](https://ref.ly/Luke4:47) · [JHN 5:13](https://ref.ly/Luke5:13) · [ACT 9:34](https://ref.ly/John9:34) · [ACT 10:38](https://ref.ly/John10:38) · [ACT 28:8](https://ref.ly/John28:8) · [HEB 12:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:13) · [JAS 5:16](https://ref.ly/Heb5:16) · [1PE 2:24](https://ref.ly/Jas2:24)

13\.66 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Change of State

to renew, to heal (a figurative extension of meaning of ἰάομαι\[a] ‘to heal,’ [23\.136](#23.136)) to cause something to change to an earlier, correct, or appropriate state

[MAT 13:15](https://ref.ly/Matt13:15) · [JHN 12:40](https://ref.ly/Luke12:40) · [ACT 28:27](https://ref.ly/John28:27) · [1PE 2:24](https://ref.ly/Jas2:24)

1 It is possible that διασῴζω is somewhat more emphatic in meaning than σῴζω. It is also possible that in a number of contexts σῴζω and διασῴζω may have the added implication of having rescued such persons from a state of illness.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 8:8; Matthew 8:13; Matthew 15:28; Mark 5:29; Luke 5:17; Luke 6:18; Luke 6:19; Luke 7:7; Luke 8:47; Luke 9:2; Luke 9:11; Luke 9:42; Luke 14:4; Luke 17:15; Luke 22:51; John 4:47; John 5:13; Acts 9:34; Acts 10:38; Acts 28:8; Hebrews 12:13; James 5:16; 1 Peter 2:24; Matthew 13:15; John 12:40; Acts 28:27

one’s own, one’s property pertaining to being the exclusive property of someone1

[MAT 9:1](https://ref.ly/Matt9:1) · [MAT 22:5](https://ref.ly/Matt22:5) · [MAT 25:14](https://ref.ly/Matt25:14) · [MAT 25:15](https://ref.ly/Matt25:15) · [MRK 4:34](https://ref.ly/Matt4:34) · [LUK 1:6](https://ref.ly/3John1:6)

58\.47 · Nature, Class, Example · Distinctive, Unique

peculiar, distinctive pertaining to that which is peculiar or distinctive to some entity

[LUK 6:44](https://ref.ly/Mark6:44) · [JHN 5:18](https://ref.ly/Luke5:18) · [ACT 1:25](https://ref.ly/John1:25) · [ACT 2:6](https://ref.ly/John2:6) · [ACT 2:8](https://ref.ly/John2:8) · [1CO 15:38](https://ref.ly/Rom15:38) · [1TI 2:6](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:6) · [1TI 6:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:15)

92\.21 · Discourse Referentials · Whom or What Spoken or Written About

individually, separately a reference to each one individually

[1CO 12:11](https://ref.ly/Rom12:11) · [TIT 2:5](https://ref.ly/2Tim2:5) · [1PE 3:5](https://ref.ly/Jas3:5)

10\.12 · Kinship Terms · Groups and Members of Groups of Persons Regarded as Related by Blood but without Special Reference to Successive Generations

**Collocation:** οἱ ἴδιοι

his own people persons who in some sense belong to a so\-called reference person

[JHN 1:11](https://ref.ly/Luke1:11) · [JHN 10:3](https://ref.ly/Luke10:3) · [JHN 10:4](https://ref.ly/Luke10:4) · [JHN 13:1](https://ref.ly/Luke13:1) · [ACT 24:23](https://ref.ly/John24:23)

28\.67 · Know · Able To Be Known

**Collocation:** κατ᾽ ἰδίαν

privately (an idiom, literally: according to that which is private) pertaining to what occurs in a private context or setting, in the sense of not being made known publicly

[MAT 14:13](https://ref.ly/Matt14:13) · [MAT 14:23](https://ref.ly/Matt14:23) · [MAT 17:1](https://ref.ly/Matt17:1) · [MAT 17:19](https://ref.ly/Matt17:19) · [MAT 20:17](https://ref.ly/Matt20:17) · [MAT 24:3](https://ref.ly/Matt24:3) · [MRK 4:34](https://ref.ly/Matt4:34) · [MRK 6:31](https://ref.ly/Matt6:31) · [MRK 6:32](https://ref.ly/Matt6:32) · [MRK 7:33](https://ref.ly/Matt7:33) · [MRK 9:2](https://ref.ly/Matt9:2) · [MRK 9:28](https://ref.ly/Matt9:28) · [MRK 13:3](https://ref.ly/Matt13:3) · [LUK 9:10](https://ref.ly/Mark9:10) · [LUK 10:23](https://ref.ly/Mark10:23) · [ACT 23:19](https://ref.ly/John23:19) · [GAL 2:2](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:2)

1 τὰ ἴδια is a substantivized form of ἴδιος\[a], occurring only in the neuter plural and meaning one’s own possessions, as in [LUK 18:28](https://ref.ly/Mark18:28), ἰδοὺ ἡμεῖς ἀφέντες τὰ ἴδια ἠκολουθήσαμέν σοι look, we have left all our possessions to follow you. Some scholars, however, interpret τὰ ἴδια in this passage to mean one’s own home. In [JHN 1:11](https://ref.ly/Luke1:11), εἰς τὰ ἴδια ἦλθεν he came into his own possessions, it is possible to understand τὰ ἴδια in the sense of his own nation.

## ἰδιώτης (id: 002404000000000)

ἰδιώτης
=======

ἰδιώτης (G2399)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 ἴδιος

27\.26 · Learn · Learn

layman, ordinary person, amateur a person who has not acquired systemic information or expertise in some field of knowledge or activity In [1CO 14:16](https://ref.ly/Rom14:16) ἰδιώτης is used to refer to a class of persons who were neither unbelievers nor fully instructed Christians, but who were inquirers or catechumens. In such a context, ἰδιώτης may be rendered as ‘ordinary, uninitiated’ (ἐπεὶ ἐὰν εὐλογῇς ἐν πνεύματι, ὁ ἀναπληρῶν τὸν τόπον τοῦ ἰδιώτου πῶς ἐρεῖ τὸ Ἀμήν ἐπὶ τῇ σῇ εὐχαριστίᾳ ‘when you give thanks to God in spirit only, how can an ordinary, uninitiated person taking part in the meeting say “Amen” to your prayer of thanksgiving’).

[ACT 4:13](https://ref.ly/John4:13) · [1CO 14:16](https://ref.ly/Rom14:16) · [1CO 14:23](https://ref.ly/Rom14:23) · [1CO 14:24](https://ref.ly/Rom14:24) · [2CO 11:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:6)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 4:13; 1 Corinthians 14:16; 1 Corinthians 14:23; 1 Corinthians 14:24; 2 Corinthians 11:6

## ἱερατεύω (id: 002411000000000)

ἱερατεύω
========

ἱερατεύω (G2407)

ἀρχιερατικός · ἀρχιερεύς · ἱερατεία · ἱεράτευμα · ἱερεύς · ἱερόθυτος · ἱερόν · ἱεροπρεπής · ἱερός · ἱεροσυλέω · ἱερουργέω · ἱερωσύνη

53\.85 · Religious Activities · Roles and Functions

to serve as a priest, to be a priest to serve as a priest in the performance of religious rites and duties In contrast with the prophet who speaks to people on behalf of God, the priest is often defined as one who represents the people before God. In reality, however, the priest is one who is primarily engaged in religious ritual and ceremony in contrast with the prophet, whose primary activity is involved in proclaiming a message. In societies in which there is no organized priesthood and where there are only medicine men or shamans, it has often been possible to translate ἱερουργέω and ἱερατεύω as simply ‘to be God’s shaman.’ Whether such an expression can be used depends very largely upon the connotations associated with shamanism.

[LUK 1:8](https://ref.ly/Mark1:8)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:8

## ἱερόθυτος (id: 002415000000000)

ἱερόθυτος
=========

ἱερόθυτος (G1494a)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ον 

|  |
| --- |

 ἱερατεύω \+ θύω

53\.21 · Religious Activities · Offering, Sacrifice

what has been sacrificed, having been sacrificed to a deity pertaining to being sacrificed to a deity In some cultures sacrificing is not practiced, and even the idea of killing an animal as a gift to a deity seems not only strange but even abhorrent. In such languages no special term is to be found for sacrifice, and it may therefore be necessary to use a phrase such as ‘to kill an animal and give it to God’ or ‘to kill an animal in honor of God.’ In such cases, however, it is obviously necessary to have some kind of supplementary note or glossary statement which will attempt to explain the significance and function of sacrifice in the Bible.

[1CO 10:28](https://ref.ly/Rom10:28)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 10:28


## ἱεροπρεπής (id: 002416000000000)

ἱεροπρεπής
==========

ἱεροπρεπής (G2412)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ές 

|  |
| --- |

 ἱερατεύω \+ πρέπει

53\.6 · Religious Activities · Religious Practice

devout, pious, religious pertaining to being devoted to a proper expression of religious beliefs1 In a number of languages the concept of ‘living a godly life’ may be best expressed as ‘to live as God would have one live’ or ‘to live like one should who believes in God’ or ‘to always do what God requires.’ In some languages, however, the only equivalent is ‘to live a good life’ or ‘to live always doing good to others.’ The shift from the focus upon religious belief to good living or being good to others results from the fact that in some religious systems there is little or no connection between religious beliefs and moral behavior.

[TIT 2:3](https://ref.ly/2Tim2:3)

1 There are no doubt certain subtle differences of meaning in this series, but it is difficult to define these distinctions on the basis of existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Titus 2:3


## ἱερός (id: 002417000000000)

ἱερός
=====

ἱερός (G2413) — ἱερόν

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ά, \-όν 

|  |
| --- |

 ἱερατεύω

53\.9 · Religious Activities · Religious Practice

holy pertaining to being appropriate for the expression of worship and reverence In [1CO 9:13](https://ref.ly/Rom9:13) the reference of the expression οἱ τὰ ἱερὰ ἐργαζόμενοι is the activities in the Temple involving the performance of various rituals.  
In a number of languages, however, it is difficult to speak of ‘holy writings’ or ‘holy activities.’ In some instances one may use an expression which refers to positive taboo, that is to say, something which has been dedicated exclusively to the service of God, but in other languages it may be necessary to use some phrase which identifies objects or activities as being ‘appropriate for worship’ or ‘characteristic of worship’ or ‘involved in worship.’

[MRK 16:8](https://ref.ly/Matt16:8) · [1CO 9:13](https://ref.ly/Rom9:13) · [2TI 3:15](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:15)

7\.16 · Constructions · Buildings

**Collocation:** ἱερόν

temple a temple or sanctuary (ναός\[a], [7\.15](#7.15)) and the surrounding consecrated area With the exception of ἱερόν in [ACT 19:27](https://ref.ly/John19:27) (a reference to the temple of Artemis in Ephesus), ἱερόν in the NT refers to the Temple in Jerusalem, including the entire Temple precinct with its buildings, courts, and storerooms.  
In a number of languages ἱερόν is rendered normally as ‘the house of God,’ or, as in [ACT 19:27](https://ref.ly/John19:27), ‘the house of the goddess Artemis.’ In a number of languages, however, there are technical terms for ‘temple,’ and these are often carefully distinguished from an expression designating a central sanctuary in which the deity is thought to dwell (ναός\[a]).  
Though in a number of contexts it is not necessary to distinguish between ἱερόν and ναός, in [MAT 21:12](https://ref.ly/Matt21:12) (and parallel passages: [MRK 11:15](https://ref.ly/Matt11:15), [LUK 19:45](https://ref.ly/Mark19:45), and [JHN 2:14](https://ref.ly/Luke2:14)) it is important to indicate this distinction, so as not to leave the impression that sacrificial animals were actually being sold inside the central sanctuary.

## ἱεροσυλέω (id: 002420000000000)

ἱεροσυλέω
=========

ἱεροσυλέω (G2416)

ἱερατεύω \+ συλάω

57\.241 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Steal, Rob

to rob temples to take by force or stealth objects from a temple It is also possible to interpret ἱεροσυλέω in [ROM 2:22](https://ref.ly/Acts2:22) as meaning ‘to commit sacrilege,’ in the sense of doing harm or damage to sacred objects in temples (see [53\.104](#53.104)).

[ROM 2:22](https://ref.ly/Acts2:22)

53\.104 · Religious Activities · Sacrilege

to commit sacrilege, to desecrate to commit sacrilege by doing harm or damage to sacred objects in temples In biblical times the damaging of valuable objects in a temple was more than simply a criminal act, since it involved a serious breach of respect for supernatural beings. Accordingly, doing harm to sacred objects in a temple would be regarded as a particularly godless deed. For another interpretation of ἱεροσυλέω in [ROM 2:22](https://ref.ly/Acts2:22), see [57\.241](#57.241).

[ROM 2:22](https://ref.ly/Acts2:22)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 2:22


## ἱερόσυλος (id: 002421000000000)

ἱερόσυλος

ἱερόσυλος (G2417)

adj

 \-ον 

|  |
| --- |

 ἱερατεύω \+ συλάω

57\.242 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Steal, Rob

[ACT 19:37](https://ref.ly/John19:37)

53\.105 · Religious Activities · Sacrilege

desecrator, one who commits sacrilege one who commits sacrilege by damaging sacred objects in temples For another interpretation of ἱερόσυλος in [ACT 19:37](https://ref.ly/John19:37), see [57\.242](#57.242).

[ACT 19:37](https://ref.ly/John19:37)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 19:37


## ἱερουργέω (id: 002422000000000)

ἱερουργέω
=========

ἱερουργέω (G2418)

ἱερατεύω \+ ἐργάζομαι

53\.85 · Religious Activities · Roles and Functions

to serve as a priest, to be a priest to serve as a priest in the performance of religious rites and duties In contrast with the prophet who speaks to people on behalf of God, the priest is often defined as one who represents the people before God. In reality, however, the priest is one who is primarily engaged in religious ritual and ceremony in contrast with the prophet, whose primary activity is involved in proclaiming a message. In societies in which there is no organized priesthood and where there are only medicine men or shamans, it has often been possible to translate ἱερουργέω and ἱερατεύω as simply ‘to be God’s shaman.’ Whether such an expression can be used depends very largely upon the connotations associated with shamanism.

[ROM 15:16](https://ref.ly/Acts15:16)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 15:16

93\.169b · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

Jesus an additional name assigned to Barabbas ([MAT 27:16](https://ref.ly/Matt27:16), [MAT 27:17](https://ref.ly/Matt27:17), apparatus) ‘Jesus’ is a Greek transliteration for the Hebrew name Joshua.

[MAT 27:16](https://ref.ly/Matt27:16) · [MAT 27:17](https://ref.ly/Matt27:17)

93\.169c · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

Joshua the son of Eliezer mentioned in the genealogy of Jesus ‘Jesus’ is a Greek transliteration for the Hebrew name Joshua.

[LUK 3:29](https://ref.ly/Mark3:29)

93\.169d · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

Jesus, Joshua an additional name assigned to Justus, a companion of Paul ‘Jesus’ is a Greek transliteration for the Hebrew name Joshua.

[COL 4:11](https://ref.ly/Phil4:11)

## ἱκανός (id: 002428000000000)

ἱκανός
======

ἱκανός (G2425) — ἱκανόν

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ή, \-όν 

|  |
| --- |

 ἱκανόω

78\.50 · Degree · Completely, Enough \[Completive Degree]

enough, sufficient a degree which is sufficient1 In some languages one can express the concept of sufficiency in [2CO 2:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:6) by introducing a negative, for example, ‘it is not necessary to punish such a person more.’ For another interpretation of ἱκανός in [2CO 2:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:6), see [78\.14](#78.14).

[2CO 2:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:6)

78\.14 · Degree · Much, Little \[Positive\-Negative Degree]

great, intense, bright (in relationship to light) a relatively high point on a scale of extent It is also possible to understand ἱκανός in [2CO 2:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:6) as ‘sufficiency’ (see [78\.50](#78.50)).

[ACT 20:37](https://ref.ly/John20:37) · [ACT 22:6](https://ref.ly/John22:6)2 · [2CO 2:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:6)

75\.2 · Adequate, Qualified

adequate, qualified (derivative of ἱκανότης ‘adequacy,’ [75\.1](#75.1)) pertaining to being adequate for something

[MAT 3:11](https://ref.ly/Matt3:11) · [MAT 8:8](https://ref.ly/Matt8:8) · [MRK 1:7](https://ref.ly/Matt1:7) · [LUK 3:16](https://ref.ly/Mark3:16) · [LUK 7:6](https://ref.ly/Mark7:6) · [1CO 15:9](https://ref.ly/Rom15:9) · [2CO 2:16](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:16) · [2CO 3:5](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:5) · [2TI 2:2](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:2)

59\.44 · Quantity · Enough, Sufficient

enough, sufficient pertaining to a quantity which is adequate for a particular purpose

[LUK 20:9](https://ref.ly/Mark20:9) · [LUK 22:38](https://ref.ly/Mark22:38) · [LUK 23:8](https://ref.ly/Mark23:8)

59\.2 · Quantity · Many, Few \[Countables]

considerable, many, quite a number of a considerable number of objects or events, probably implying what could be expected under the circumstances

[LUK 8:32](https://ref.ly/Mark8:32) · [LUK 23:9](https://ref.ly/Mark23:9) · [ACT 9:23](https://ref.ly/John9:23) · [ACT 9:43](https://ref.ly/John9:43) · [ACT 12:12](https://ref.ly/John12:12) · [ACT 14:21](https://ref.ly/John14:21) · [ACT 18:18](https://ref.ly/John18:18) · [ACT 19:19](https://ref.ly/John19:19) · [ACT 20:8](https://ref.ly/John20:8) · [ACT 27:7](https://ref.ly/John27:7) · [1CO 11:30](https://ref.ly/Rom11:30)

59\.12 · Quantity · Much, Little \[Masses, Collectives, Extensions]

large, considerable, extensive a relatively large quantity, probably implying what could be expected under the circumstances

[MAT 28:12](https://ref.ly/Matt28:12) · [MRK 10:46](https://ref.ly/Matt10:46) · [LUK 7:12](https://ref.ly/Mark7:12) · [LUK 8:27](https://ref.ly/Mark8:27) · [ACT 8:11](https://ref.ly/John8:11) · [ACT 11:24](https://ref.ly/John11:24) · [ACT 11:26](https://ref.ly/John11:26) · [ACT 14:3](https://ref.ly/John14:3) · [ACT 19:26](https://ref.ly/John19:26) · [ACT 20:11](https://ref.ly/John20:11) · [ACT 27:9](https://ref.ly/John27:9)

25\.96 · Attitudes and Emotions · Acceptable To, To Be Pleased With

**Collocation:** ποιέω τὸ ἱκανόν

to act in a pleasing manner, to please (an idiom, literally: to do what is enough) to cause someone to be pleased by doing what will satisfy

[MRK 15:15](https://ref.ly/Matt15:15)

57\.169 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Pay, Price, Cost

**Collocation:** ἱκανόν

bond, bail, the amount of money required for release the amount of money required to release someone who has been held in custody It may be necessary in a number of languages to be very specific about the meaning of ἱκανόν, for example, ‘the amount of money which had to be paid in order for someone to be released from arrest.’

[ACT 17:9](https://ref.ly/John17:9)

1 Compare ἱκανός\[b] meaning a relatively high point on a scale of extent ([78\.14](#78.14)) and also ἱκανός\[e] ([59\.2](#59.2)) and ἱκανός\[f] ([59\.12](#59.12)) referring to quantity. 2 ACT 22:6 ἱκανός as an expression of degree also occurs with the meaning of ‘enough’ (see [78\.50](#78.50)), but the meaning of ‘enough’ or ‘sufficient’ would not be appropriate in [ACT 22:6](https://ref.ly/John22:6).

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 2:6; Acts 20:37; Acts 22:6; Matthew 3:11; Matthew 8:8; Mark 1:7; Luke 3:16; Luke 7:6; 1 Corinthians 15:9; 2 Corinthians 2:16; 2 Corinthians 3:5; 2 Timothy 2:2; Luke 20:9; Luke 22:38; Luke 23:8; Luke 8:32; Luke 23:9; Acts 9:23; Acts 9:43; Acts 12:12; Acts 14:21; Acts 18:18; Acts 19:19; Acts 20:8; Acts 27:7; 1 Corinthians 11:30; Matthew 28:12; Mark 10:46; Luke 7:12; Luke 8:27; Acts 8:11; Acts 11:24; Acts 11:26; Acts 14:3; Acts 19:26; Acts 20:11; Acts 27:9; Mark 15:15; Acts 17:9

## ἱλάσκομαι (id: 002436000000000)

ἱλάσκομαι
=========

ἱλάσκομαι (G2433)

ἱλασμός · ἱλαστήριον

40\.9 · Reconciliation, Forgiveness · Forgiveness

to forgive to forgive, with the focus upon the instrumentality or the means by which forgiveness is accomplished

[HEB 2:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:17)

88\.75 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Mercy, Merciless

to show mercy, to show compassion to show compassion and concern for someone in difficulty, despite that person's having committed a moral offense In rendering ἱλάσκομι in [LUK 18:13](https://ref.ly/Mark18:13) it is inadequate simply to indicate an attitude on the part of God. Having mercy or showing compassion must involve some act of kindness or concern.

[LUK 18:13](https://ref.ly/Mark18:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 2:17; Luke 18:13


## ἱλασμός (id: 002437000000000)

ἱλασμός
=======

ἱλασμός (G2434)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-οῦ 

|  |
| --- |

 ἱλάσκομαι

40\.12 · Reconciliation, Forgiveness · Forgiveness

the means of forgiveness, expiation the means by which sins are forgiven Though some traditional translations render ἱλαστήριον as ‘propitiation,’ this involves a wrong interpretation of the term in question. Propitiation is essentially a process by which one does a favor to a person in order to make him or her favorably disposed, but in the NT God is never the object of propitiation since he is already on the side of people. ἱλασμός and ἱλαστήριον\[a] denote the means of forgiveness and not propitiation.

[1JN 2:2](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:2) · [1JN 4:10](https://ref.ly/2Pet4:10)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 John 2:2; 1 John 4:10

## ἱμάς (id: 002441000000000)

ἱμάς
====

ἱμάς (G2438)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-άντος

6\.20 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Binding and Fastening

strap, thong leather strap or thong (used in binding sandals or shoes and as thongs in a whip) In a number of languages ἱμάς\[a] may be translated as ‘leather string’ or ‘strip of leather.’ In [JHN 1:27](https://ref.ly/Luke1:27) the term may be absorbed within the total expression, for example, worthy to untie his sandals (implying the untying of the straps with which the sandals were bound).  
In [ACT 22:25](https://ref.ly/John22:25) the clause ὡς δὲ προέτειναν αὐτὸν τοῖς ἱμᾶσιν may be interpreted as ‘they tied him up with thongs’ or as ‘they tied him up for whipping,’ in which case ἱμᾶσιν would refer to an event, not to an object (see [19\.9](#19.9)).

[MRK 1:7](https://ref.ly/Matt1:7) · [LUK 3:16](https://ref.ly/Mark3:16) · [JHN 1:27](https://ref.ly/Luke1:27) · [ACT 22:25](https://ref.ly/John22:25)

19\.9 · Physical Impact · Hit, Strike

whipping, flogging act of beating severely with a whip It is also possible to interpret ἱμάς in [ACT 22:25](https://ref.ly/John22:25) as the thongs with which Paul was tied up (see [6\.20](#6.20)).

[ACT 22:25](https://ref.ly/John22:25)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 1:7; Luke 3:16; John 1:27; Acts 22:25

6\.172 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

cloak, coat, robe any type of outer garment1 The choice of an equivalent for these terms relating to ‘outer garments’ will depend largely upon the specific context and the usage in each receptor language. The most common equivalent is a term meaning ‘coat.’

1 There are no doubt certain minor distinctions in meaning for the four terms in [6\.172](#6.172), but it is impossible to determine the distinctive features on the basis of existing contexts. There are considerable differences of opinion about φαιλόνης, regarded by many as a loan word from Latin paenula.

89\.49 · Relations · Result

so as a result, that, so that a marker of result, though in some cases implying an underlying or indirect purpose In some languages it is difficult to mark a result clause in a context such as [JHN 9:2](https://ref.ly/Luke9:2). This may be done, however, by restructuring the statement as ‘he was born blind; therefore, who sinned? Did this man sin or did his parents sin?’

90\.22 · Case · Content

that a marker of the content of discourse, particularly if and when purpose is implied2 An expression of command is implicit in this passage in [EPH 5:33](https://ref.ly/Gal5:33), and therefore one may interpret this clause with ἵνα as being a matter of content.

91\.15 · Discourse Markers · Markers of Identificational and Explanatory Clauses \[Epexegetical]

that, namely, that is, namely that a marker of identificational and explanatory clauses

[MAT 5:29](https://ref.ly/Matt5:29) · [LUK 1:43](https://ref.ly/Mark1:43) · [LUK 22:30](https://ref.ly/Mark22:30) · [JHN 6:29](https://ref.ly/Luke6:29) · [JHN 6:39](https://ref.ly/Luke6:39) · [JHN 6:40](https://ref.ly/Luke6:40) · [JHN 11:50](https://ref.ly/Luke11:50) · [JHN 15:8](https://ref.ly/Luke15:8) · [JHN 15:12](https://ref.ly/Luke15:12) · [JHN 15:13](https://ref.ly/Luke15:13) · [JHN 17:3](https://ref.ly/Luke17:3) · [JHN 18:39](https://ref.ly/Luke18:39) · [EPH 6:22](https://ref.ly/Gal6:22) · [COL 4:8](https://ref.ly/Phil4:8) · [JAS 1:4](https://ref.ly/Heb1:4) · [1JN 1:9](https://ref.ly/2Pet1:9) · [1JN 3:1](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:1)

1 ἵνα\[a] and ὅπως\[b] seem to have similar meanings and in some contexts appear to be substituted one for the other for stylistic purposes. It is, of course, possible that even in the meaning of purpose ὅπως\[b] suggests something of the manner or way in which the purpose is to be realized, but it is impossible on the basis of existing contexts to make a clear distinction between ἵνα\[a] and ὅπως\[b] when they serve as markers of purpose. 2 In a number of instances, a marker of direct discourse is not represented in translation, particularly if what is indirect discourse in the Greek text is rendered as direct discourse.

## ἰός (id: 002449000000000)

ἰός
===

ἰός (G2447)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-οῦ 

|  |
| --- |

 κατιόομαι

8\.74 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Physiological Products of the Body

venom, poison (used especially of the venom of snakes) the poisonous secretion of some animals

[ROM 3:13](https://ref.ly/Acts3:13) · [JAS 3:8](https://ref.ly/Heb3:8)

2\.60 · Natural Substances · Metals

rust, tarnish the substance resulting from the slow oxidation of metals (rust in the case of iron and tarnish in the case of gold and silver) Pure gold is not affected significantly by oxidation, but much of the gold of the ancient world was not pure, and therefore oxidation and resulting tarnish did take place. However, in most languages it is inappropriate to speak of ‘rust’ as occurring with gold and silver. If there is no satisfactory term to indicate the deterioration in gold and silver resulting in extreme tarnish, it may be possible to translate [JAS 5:3](https://ref.ly/Heb5:3) as ‘your gold and silver will be ruined and this will serve as a witness against you.’

[JAS 5:3](https://ref.ly/Heb5:3)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 3:13; James 3:8; James 5:3

 \-ου

93\.172 · (ου m) · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-αία, \-αῖον

93\.170 · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

a Jewess (derivative of Ἰούδας\[a] ‘Judah,’ [93\.173](#93.173), and Ἰούδας\[c] ‘Judah,’ [93\.488](#93.488))1 the ethnic name of a woman belonging to the Jewish nation

## ἵππος (id: 002464000000000)

ἵππος
=====

ἵππος (G2462)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 ἱππεύς · ἱππικόν

4\.29 · Animals · Animals

horse large domesticated solid\-hoofed quadruped; Equus caballus; stockily built in comparison to today’s horses, with shorter heads and thicker necks; about 122–142 cm tall, and 2\.1 m long; coat varies from dark to pale brown; eats plants; used in battle, both to ride and for pulling chariots; symbolic of military might; associated with the sun, which was said to ride across the sky in a chariot Since horses are widely distributed in the world (at least knowledge about them is widespread), it is rarely difficult to obtain a satisfactory term. In some instances, however, expressions designating horses may seem rather strange. For example, in Sediq, a language spoken in Taiwan, a horse is literally ‘a soldier’s cow.’

[JAS 3:3](https://ref.ly/Heb3:3) · [REV 6:2](https://ref.ly/Jude6:2) · [REV 6:4](https://ref.ly/Jude6:4) · [REV 6:5](https://ref.ly/Jude6:5) · [REV 6:8](https://ref.ly/Jude6:8) · [REV 9:7](https://ref.ly/Jude9:7) · [REV 9:9](https://ref.ly/Jude9:9) · [REV 9:17](https://ref.ly/Jude9:17) · [REV 9:17](https://ref.ly/Jude9:17) · [REV 9:19](https://ref.ly/Jude9:19) · [REV 14:20](https://ref.ly/Jude14:20) · [REV 18:13](https://ref.ly/Jude18:13) · [REV 19:11](https://ref.ly/Jude19:11) · [REV 19:14](https://ref.ly/Jude19:14) · [REV 19:18](https://ref.ly/Jude19:18) · [REV 19:19](https://ref.ly/Jude19:19) · [REV 19:21](https://ref.ly/Jude19:21)

* **Associated Passages:** James 3:3; Revelation 6:2; Revelation 6:4; Revelation 6:5; Revelation 6:8; Revelation 9:7; Revelation 9:9; Revelation 9:17; Revelation 9:19; Revelation 14:20; Revelation 18:13; Revelation 19:11; Revelation 19:14; Revelation 19:18; Revelation 19:19; Revelation 19:21


## ἶρις (id: 002465000000000)

ἶρις
====

ἶρις (G2463)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ιδος

1\.38 · Geographical Objects and Features · Atmospheric Objects

rainbow or halo a circular or semicircular band of light, whether colored or not1 In [REV 4:3](https://ref.ly/Jude4:3) and [REV 10:1](https://ref.ly/Jude10:1) (the only occurrences of ἶρις in the NT) the reference may be either to a rainbow or to a halo. The meaning of ‘rainbow’ may be expressed in some languages as ‘a bow of light’ or ‘a curve of light’ or even ‘a ribbon of light.’ The meaning of ‘halo’ is usually expressed as ‘a circle of light’ or ‘a wreath of light’ or ‘a band of light encircling,’ followed by the object which the band of light encircles.

[REV 4:3](https://ref.ly/Jude4:3) · [REV 10:1](https://ref.ly/Jude10:1)

1 It would also be possible to classify ἶρις rainbow or halo as being an event rather than an object, but in view of the relatively fixed Gestalt of this phenomenon, it is probably more satisfactory from the standpoint of an emic classification to regard ἶρις as an object.

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 4:3; Revelation 10:1

## ἱστορέω (id: 002477000000000)

ἱστορέω
=======

ἱστορέω (G2477)

34\.52 · Association · Visit

to visit and get information to visit, with the purpose of obtaining information1 In rendering ‘to get information from him’ it may be more satisfactory to say ‘to learn something from him’ or ‘to have him tell me what I needed to know.’

[GAL 1:18](https://ref.ly/2Cor1:18)

1 ἱστορέω can perhaps best be interpreted as combining two different domains: (1\) the domain of Association (34\) involving visiting and (2\) the domain of Communication (33\) involving the soliciting of information. This is a typical example of a meaning which overlaps two domains.

* **Associated Passages:** Galatians 1:18

## ἰσχύς (id: 002479000000000)

ἰσχύς
=====

ἰσχύς (G2479)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ύος 

|  |
| --- |

 ἰσχύω

74\.8 · Able, Capable

capability, strength exceptional capability, with the probable implication of personal potential In a number of languages the expression ‘to love the Lord with one’s strength,’ in the sense of physical strength, is meaningless, and therefore it may be necessary to translate ‘love the Lord your God as completely as you can.’ It is important to note that in a passage such as [MRK 12:30](https://ref.ly/Matt12:30) the terms in the series καρδίαψυχήδιάνοια, and ἰσχύς do not refer to completely different parts or aspects of human personality; rather, the four are combined to emphasize the totality of the individual. In some languages the equivalent way of expressing this comprehensive aspect of personality is ‘to love him completely with all you feel and all you think.’

[MRK 12:30](https://ref.ly/Matt12:30) · [MRK 12:33](https://ref.ly/Matt12:33) · [LUK 10:27](https://ref.ly/Mark10:27)

79\.62 · Features of Objects · Strong, Weak

strength the quality of physical strength

## ἰσχύω (id: 002480000000000)

ἰσχύω
=====

ἰσχύω (G2480)

διϊσχυρίζομαι · ἐνισχύω · ἐξισχύω · ἐπισχύω · ἰσχυρός · ἰσχύς · κατισχύω

74\.9 · Able, Capable

to be able to, to have the strength to, to be very capable of (derivative of ἰσχύς\[a] ‘capability,’ [74\.8](#74.8)) to have special personal ability to do or experience something1

[MAT 8:28](https://ref.ly/Matt8:28) · [MAT 26:40](https://ref.ly/Matt26:40) · [MRK 5:4](https://ref.ly/Matt5:4) · [MRK 9:18](https://ref.ly/Matt9:18) · [MRK 14:37](https://ref.ly/Matt14:37) · [LUK 6:48](https://ref.ly/Mark6:48) · [LUK 8:43](https://ref.ly/Mark8:43) · [LUK 13:24](https://ref.ly/Mark13:24) · [LUK 14:6](https://ref.ly/Mark14:6) · [LUK 14:29](https://ref.ly/Mark14:29) · [LUK 14:30](https://ref.ly/Mark14:30) · [LUK 20:26](https://ref.ly/Mark20:26) · [ACT 6:10](https://ref.ly/John6:10) · [ACT 15:10](https://ref.ly/John15:10) · [ACT 25:7](https://ref.ly/John25:7) · [ACT 27:16](https://ref.ly/John27:16) · [GAL 5:6](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:6) · [PHP 4:13](https://ref.ly/Eph4:13) · [HEB 9:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:17) · [JAS 5:16](https://ref.ly/Heb5:16) · [REV 12:8](https://ref.ly/Jude12:8)

79\.64 · Features of Objects · Strong, Weak

to be strong enough to, to be able to, to have the strength to to be physically strong enough for some purpose

[MAT 5:13](https://ref.ly/Matt5:13) · [LUK 16:3](https://ref.ly/Mark16:3) · [JHN 21:6](https://ref.ly/Luke21:6) · [ACT 19:16](https://ref.ly/John19:16) · [ACT 19:20](https://ref.ly/John19:20)

23\.130 · Physiological Processes and States · Health, Vigor, Strength

to be healthy a state of being healthy, with the implication of robustness and vigor

[MAT 9:12](https://ref.ly/Matt9:12) · [MRK 2:17](https://ref.ly/Matt2:17)

1 Note that ἰσχύω\[a] may occur without a verb complement, thus making possible a translation such as to be able to do or to be able to prevail as in [REV 12:8](https://ref.ly/Jude12:8) (καὶ οὐκ ἴσχυσεν and he was not able to prevail). In some languages, however, it may be better to render this expression in [REV 12:8](https://ref.ly/Jude12:8) as he was defeated.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 8:28; Matthew 26:40; Mark 5:4; Mark 9:18; Mark 14:37; Luke 6:48; Luke 8:43; Luke 13:24; Luke 14:6; Luke 14:29; Luke 14:30; Luke 20:26; Acts 6:10; Acts 15:10; Acts 25:7; Acts 27:16; Galatians 5:6; Philippians 4:13; Hebrews 9:17; James 5:16; Revelation 12:8; Matthew 5:13; Luke 16:3; John 21:6; Acts 19:16; Acts 19:20; Matthew 9:12; Mark 2:17


## ἴσως (id: 002481000000000)

ἴσως
====

ἴσως (G2481)

adv 

|  |
| --- |

 ἴσος

71\.11 · Mode · Probable, Improbable

probably, likely pertaining to an event having a high degree of probability In view of the misjudgment implied in [LUK 20:13](https://ref.ly/Mark20:13), a number of translators have rendered ἴσως as simply ‘perhaps’ or ‘maybe,’ though the Greek term ἴσως would certainly imply a considerably higher degree of hope for a successful outcome.

[LUK 20:13](https://ref.ly/Mark20:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 20:13

## ἰχθύς (id: 002486000000000)

ἰχθύς
=====

ἰχθύς (G2486)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ύος 

|  |
| --- |

 ἰχθύδιον

4\.59 · Animals · Fishes and Other Sea Creatures

sea creature, fish any creature living in the sea Though all languages have terms to designate at least certain kinds of fish, there are frequently important distinctions between varieties. In a number of instances distinctions are made between fish which have scales and those which do not (an important distinction in the OT, since it constituted the basis for distinguishing between ‘clean’ or ‘unclean’ varieties). In other languages the distinction may be made between fresh water and salt water fish, while in still other languages a clear distinction is made between edible and inedible fish.  
Some languages also distinguish between fish which are still alive in the water and those which have been caught and are in various stages of preparation for being eaten. In [MAT 7:10](https://ref.ly/Matt7:10) ἰχθύς may refer to a piece of fish ready to be eaten.

[MAT 7:10](https://ref.ly/Matt7:10) · [MAT 14:17](https://ref.ly/Matt14:17) · [MAT 14:19](https://ref.ly/Matt14:19) · [MAT 15:36](https://ref.ly/Matt15:36) · [MAT 17:27](https://ref.ly/Matt17:27) · [MRK 6:38](https://ref.ly/Matt6:38) · [MRK 6:41](https://ref.ly/Matt6:41) · [MRK 6:41](https://ref.ly/Matt6:41) · [MRK 6:43](https://ref.ly/Matt6:43) · [LUK 5:6](https://ref.ly/Mark5:6) · [LUK 5:9](https://ref.ly/Mark5:9) · [LUK 9:13](https://ref.ly/Mark9:13) · [LUK 9:16](https://ref.ly/Mark9:16) · [LUK 11:11](https://ref.ly/Mark11:11) · [LUK 11:11](https://ref.ly/Mark11:11) · [LUK 24:42](https://ref.ly/Mark24:42) · [JHN 21:6](https://ref.ly/Luke21:6) · [JHN 21:8](https://ref.ly/Luke21:8) · [JHN 21:11](https://ref.ly/Luke21:11) · [1CO 15:39](https://ref.ly/Rom15:39)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 7:10; Matthew 14:17; Matthew 14:19; Matthew 15:36; Matthew 17:27; Mark 6:38; Mark 6:41; Mark 6:43; Luke 5:6; Luke 5:9; Luke 9:13; Luke 9:16; Luke 11:11; Luke 24:42; John 21:6; John 21:8; John 21:11; 1 Corinthians 15:39
